NARRATOR: Whiskey. Two almost-empty glasses on the counter, third bottle in a week. The sink overflows with dishes, one mug still crusted with coffee and something worse. Luke’s hands are steady, even now, dabbing antiseptic onto Matt’s ribs—skin scored raw under the tape. Jessica leans against the fridge, arms crossed, a half-smoked cigarette curling upward between her fingers. Her eyes stay fixed on the blood, not the men.
JESSICA JONES: He’s gonna live. I don’t know whether to thank you or call Animal Control. Still not sure why the hell you thought I was the one to ask.
LUKE CAGE: If it were you, Jess, he'd already be there. Don't matter how blind he is. What's it cost you to return that?
JESSICA JONES: I don’t do charity, and I don’t do martyr shit. But if you’re still breathing tomorrow, I’ll think about it.
LUKE CAGE: You can radiate all you want, Jess. Smoke screen or not, you know what’s right here.
MATT MURDOCK: I don’t need convincing. But stalling doesn’t drag me out either. Decide, or I do."  

It’s their deadlock, but the runway’s burned too short. My head turns just slightly towards the sound of the door, the exit, car debate stopped cold in waiting silence.
NARRATOR: Silence, weighted and sharp. Matt straightens, favoring his unbandaged side, the scrape of his cane against the floor all the sound there is. Luke doesn’t move, shoulders locked, jaw tight. Jessica takes one last drag; the ember flares, but her feet stay rooted. None of them look at the door. Only Matt does.
JESSICA JONES: Fine. But don’t make me regret it.
JESSICA JONES: Let’s get this over with.
JESSICA JONES: Whatever happens, you owe me more than a drink.
JESSICA JONES: Let’s move. You bleed on my boots, I’m billing you.
JESSICA JONES: Let’s see how deep this shit goes. Keep up.
JESSICA JONES: Let’s get this over with. You’re on my time now.
NARRATOR: She stubs the cigarette out on the counter, the sizzle cutting through the stillness. 'Fine,' hangs in the air even if it isn’t said. When she pulls on her jacket, Luke shifts, half a step forward, then back. He doesn’t follow. The door shuts behind them, Matt’s weight haunting her shoulder.
